     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Observation_decks">
       Observation decks
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The Empire State Building has one of the most popular outdoor observatories in the world, having been visited by over 110 million people. The 86th-floor observation deck offers impressive 360-degree views of the city. There is a second observation deck on the 102nd floor that is open to the public. It was closed in 1999, but reopened in November 2005. It is completely enclosed and much smaller than the first one; it may be closed on high-traffic days. Tourists may pay to visit the observation deck on the 86th floor and an additional amount for the 102nd floor.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_72-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-72">
        [70]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The lines to enter the observation decks, according to
      <a href="/wiki/Cond%C3%A9_Nast_Traveler" title="Condé Nast Traveler">
       Concierge.com
      </a>
      , are "as legendary as the building itself:" there are five of them: the sidewalk line, the lobby elevator line, the ticket purchase line, the second elevator line, and the line to get off the elevator and onto the observation deck.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        [71]
       </a>
      </sup>
      For an extra fee tourists can skip to the front of the line.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_72-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-72">
        [70]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Empire State Building makes more money from tickets sales for its observation decks than it does from renting office space.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DaRo_23Apr2012_74-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DaRo_23Apr2012-74">
        [72]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The skyscraper's observation deck plays host to several cinematic, television, and literary classics including,
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/An_Affair_To_Remember" title="An Affair To Remember">
        An Affair To Remember
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/On_the_Town_(film)" title="On the Town (film)">
        On the Town
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Love_Affair_(1994_film)" title="Love Affair (1994 film)">
        Love Affair
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Sleepless_in_Seattle" title="Sleepless in Seattle">
        Sleepless in Seattle
       </a>
      </i>
      . In the Latin American literary classic, Giannina
      <a href="/wiki/Braschi%27s_Empire_of_Dreams" title="Braschi's Empire of Dreams">
       Braschi's Empire of Dreams
      </a>
      the observation deck is the site of a pastoral revolution; shepherds take over the City of New York.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marting_167.E2.80.93182_75-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Marting_167.E2.80.93182-75">
        [73]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The deck was also the site of a publicity-stunt Martian invasion in an episode of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/I_Love_Lucy" title="I Love Lucy">
        I Love Lucy
       </a>
      </i>
      ("Lucy Is Envious", season 3, episode 25).
     </p>
     <div style="clear:both;">
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:2008px;">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="">
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Skyline-New-York-City.jpg" title="A panoramic view of New York City from the 86th-floor observation deck of the Empire State Building, spring 2005">
         <img alt="" data-file-height="740" data-file-width="7979" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Skyline-New-York-City.jpg/2000px-Skyline-New-York-City.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Skyline-New-York-City.jpg/3000px-Skyline-New-York-City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Skyline-New-York-City.jpg/4000px-Skyline-New-York-City.jpg 2x" width="2000"/>
        </a>
       </div>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Skyline-New-York-City.jpg" title="File:Skyline-New-York-City.jpg">
         </a>
        </div>
        <div align="center">
         A panoramic view of New York City from the 86th-floor observation deck of the Empire State Building, spring 2005
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="New_York_Skyride">
       New York Skyride
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The Empire State Building also has a
      <a href="/wiki/Motion_simulator" title="Motion simulator">
       motion simulator
      </a>
      attraction located on the 2nd floor. Opened in 1994 as a complement to the observation deck, the New York Sky ride (or NY Sky ride) is a simulated aerial tour over the city. The cinematic presentation lasts approximately 25 minutes. As of May 2013, tickets are Adults $57, Children $42, Seniors $49.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_of_the_Empire_State_Building_from_Macy%27s.jpg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1944" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/View_of_the_Empire_State_Building_from_Macy%27s.jpg/200px-View_of_the_Empire_State_Building_from_Macy%27s.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/View_of_the_Empire_State_Building_from_Macy%27s.jpg/300px-View_of_the_Empire_State_Building_from_Macy%27s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/View_of_the_Empire_State_Building_from_Macy%27s.jpg/400px-View_of_the_Empire_State_Building_from_Macy%27s.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         View from
         <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy's">
          Macy's
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Empire_State_Building_background.jpg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Empire_State_Building_background.jpg/200px-Empire_State_Building_background.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Empire_State_Building_background.jpg/300px-Empire_State_Building_background.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Empire_State_Building_background.jpg/400px-Empire_State_Building_background.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         Night view from the same street-corner
        </div>
       </div>
       <div style="clear:left">
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Since its opening, the ride has gone through two incarnations. The original version, which ran from 1994 until around 2002, featured
      <a href="/wiki/James_Doohan" title="James Doohan">
       James Doohan
      </a>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series" title="Star Trek: The Original Series">
        Star Trek's
       </a>
      </i>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montgomery_Scott" title="Montgomery Scott">
       Scotty
      </a>
      , as the airplane's pilot, who humorously tried to keep the flight under control during a storm, with the tour taking an unexpected route through the subway, Coney Island, and FAO Schwartz, among other places. After the September 11 attacks in 2001, however, the ride was closed, and an updated version debuted in mid-2002 with actor
      <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Bacon" title="Kevin Bacon">
       Kevin Bacon
      </a>
      as the pilot. The new version of the narration attempted to make the attraction more educational, and included some minor post-9/11 patriotic undertones with retrospective footage of the World Trade Center. The new flight also goes haywire, but this segment is much shorter than in the original.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Lights">
       Lights
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      In 1964, floodlights were added to illuminate the top of the building at night.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        [74]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Since 1976 the spire has been lit in colors chosen to match seasonal and other events, such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Patrick%27s_Day" title="St. Patrick's Day">
       St. Patrick's Day
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">
       Christmas
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(United_States)" title="Independence Day (United States)">
       Independence Day
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bastille_Day" title="Bastille Day">
       Bastille Day
      </a>
      . After the eightieth birthday and subsequent death of
      <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">
       Frank Sinatra
      </a>
      , for example, the building was bathed in blue light to represent the singer's nickname "Ol' Blue Eyes". After the death of actress
      <a href="/wiki/Fay_Wray" title="Fay Wray">
       Fay Wray
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(1933_film)" title="King Kong (1933 film)">
        King Kong
       </a>
      </i>
      ) in late 2004, the building stood in complete darkness for 15 minutes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        [75]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The floodlights bathed the building in red, white, and blue for several months after the destruction of the World Trade Center, then reverted to the standard schedule.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lightingSchedule_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-lightingSchedule-78">
        [76]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On June 4, 2002, the Empire State Building donned purple and gold (the royal colors of
      <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">
       Elizabeth II
      </a>
      ), in thanks for the United Kingdom playing the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Star_Spangled_Banner" title="Star Spangled Banner">
       Star Spangled Banner
      </a>
      during the
      <a href="/wiki/Guard_Mounting" title="Guard Mounting">
       Changing of the Guard
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">
       Buckingham Palace
      </a>
      on September 12, 2001 (a show of support after the
      <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">
       September 11 attacks
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        [77]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This would also be shown after the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westminster_Dog_Show" title="Westminster Dog Show">
       Westminster Dog Show
      </a>
      . Traditionally, in addition to the standard schedule, the building will be lit in the colors of New York's sports teams on the nights they have home games (orange, blue and white for the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">
       New York Knicks
      </a>
      , red, white and blue for the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Rangers" title="New York Rangers">
       New York Rangers
      </a>
      , and so on). The first weekend in June finds the building bathed in green light for the
      <a href="/wiki/Belmont_Stakes" title="Belmont Stakes">
       Belmont Stakes
      </a>
      held in nearby Belmont Park. The building is illuminated in tennis-ball yellow during the
      <a href="/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">
       US Open
      </a>
      tennis tournament in late August and early September. It was twice lit in scarlet to support nearby
      <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University" title="Rutgers University">
       Rutgers University
      </a>
      : once for a
      <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">
       football
      </a>
      game against the
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Louisville" title="University of Louisville">
       University of Louisville
      </a>
      on November 9, 2006, and again on April 3, 2007 when the women's basketball team played in the national championship game.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        [78]
       </a>
      </sup>
      On January 13, 2012, the building was lit in red, orange, and yellow to honor the 60th anniversary of
      <a href="/wiki/NBC_News" title="NBC News">
       NBC
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Today_(U.S._TV_program)" title="Today (U.S. TV program)">
       <i>
        The Today Show
       </i>
      </a>
      making it the first time the building was illuminated to honor a television program. From June 1 to 3, 2012, the building was lit in blue and white, the colors of the
      <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Israel" title="Flag of Israel">
       Israeli flag
      </a>
      , in honor of the 49th annual
      <a href="/wiki/Celebrate_Israel_Parade" title="Celebrate Israel Parade">
       Celebrate Israel Parade
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        [79]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During 2012, the building's
      <a href="/wiki/Metal-halide_lamp" title="Metal-halide lamp">
       metal halide
      </a>
      lamps and floodlights were replaced with
      <a href="/wiki/Light-emitting_diode" title="Light-emitting diode">
       LED
      </a>
      fixtures, increasing the available colors from nine to over 16 million. The computer-controlled system allows the building to be illuminated in ways that were unable to be done previously with plastic gels. For instance, on November 6, 2012,
      <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">
       CNN
      </a>
      used the top of the Empire State Building as a scoreboard for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_United_States_presidential_election" title="2012 United States presidential election">
       2012 United States presidential election
      </a>
      . When incumbent president
      <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">
       Barack Obama
      </a>
      had reached the 270 electoral votes necessary to win re-election, the lights turned blue. Had Republican challenger
      <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">
       Mitt Romney
      </a>
      won, the building would have been lit red.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        [80]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Also, on November 26, 2012, the building had its first ever synchronized light show, using music from recording artist
      <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">
       Alicia Keys
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        [81]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        [82]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Those wishing to hear the music could tune to certain radio stations in the New York area. A video of the performance was posted online the next day.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        [83]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2013 the lights were changed to
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">
        Financial Times
       </a>
      </i>
      pink.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        [84]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the run-up week to
      <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVIII" title="Super Bowl XLVIII">
       Super Bowl XLVIII
      </a>
      held at
      <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Stadium" title="MetLife Stadium">
       MetLife Stadium
      </a>
      on February 2, 2014, the building was lit in a contest sponsored by the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">
       National Football League
      </a>
      's wireless partner,
      <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Wireless" title="Verizon Wireless">
       Verizon Wireless
      </a>
      to determine both the winner and fan support for the two teams via their team colors in the game through the #WhosGonnaWin
      <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">
       Twitter
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Hashtag" title="Hashtag">
       hashtag
      </a>
      , either the "action green" and navy blue of the
      <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks" title="Seattle Seahawks">
       Seattle Seahawks
      </a>
      or orange and blue of the
      <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">
       Denver Broncos
      </a>
      , along with a light show during the game's halftime.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        [85]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Height_records_and_comparisons">
       Height records and comparisons
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_York_Bldg._Height_Comparison.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="633" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/New_York_Bldg._Height_Comparison.svg/250px-New_York_Bldg._Height_Comparison.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/New_York_Bldg._Height_Comparison.svg/375px-New_York_Bldg._Height_Comparison.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/New_York_Bldg._Height_Comparison.svg/500px-New_York_Bldg._Height_Comparison.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_York_Bldg._Height_Comparison.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Height comparison of New York City buildings, with Empire State second from left
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Building_and_ship_comparison_to_the_Pentagon2.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1000" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Building_and_ship_comparison_to_the_Pentagon2.svg/250px-Building_and_ship_comparison_to_the_Pentagon2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Building_and_ship_comparison_to_the_Pentagon2.svg/375px-Building_and_ship_comparison_to_the_Pentagon2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Building_and_ship_comparison_to_the_Pentagon2.svg/500px-Building_and_ship_comparison_to_the_Pentagon2.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Building_and_ship_comparison_to_the_Pentagon2.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Size comparison in relation to
        <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">
         The Pentagon
        </a>
        . The Pentagon is 431 meters (1,414 ft) for comparison. The Empire State Building is in light gray.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Empire State Building remained the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_and_structures_in_the_world" title="List of tallest buildings and structures in the world">
       tallest man-made structure
      </a>
      in the world for 23 years before it was surpassed by the
      <a href="/wiki/Griffin_Television_Tower_Oklahoma" title="Griffin Television Tower Oklahoma">
       Griffin Television Tower Oklahoma
      </a>
      (KWTV Mast) in 1954. It was also the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_freestanding_structures_in_the_world" title="List of tallest freestanding structures in the world">
       tallest free-standing structure in the world
      </a>
      for 36 years before it was surpassed by the
      <a href="/wiki/Ostankino_Tower" title="Ostankino Tower">
       Ostankino Tower
      </a>
      in 1967.
     </p>
     <p>
      The longest world record held by the Empire State Building was for the tallest skyscraper (to structural height), which it held for 42 years until it was surpassed by the
      <a href="/wiki/One_World_Trade_Center#Original_building" title="One World Trade Center">
       North Tower
      </a>
      of the World Trade Center in 1972. An early-1970s proposal to dismantle the spire and replace it with an additional 11 floors, which would have brought the building's height to 1,494 feet (455 m) and made it once again the world's tallest at the time, was considered but ultimately rejected.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        [86]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      With the destruction of the World Trade Center in the
      <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">
       September 11 attacks
      </a>
      , the Empire State Building again became the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_New_York_City" title="List of tallest buildings in New York City">
       tallest building in New York City
      </a>
      , and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_world" title="List of tallest buildings in the world">
       second-tallest building in the Americas
      </a>
      , surpassed only by the
      <a href="/wiki/Willis_Tower" title="Willis Tower">
       Willis Tower
      </a>
      in Chicago. It is currently the fifth-tallest, surpassed by the Willis Tower, the
      <a href="/wiki/Trump_International_Hotel_and_Tower_(Chicago)" title="Trump International Hotel and Tower (Chicago)">
       Trump International Hotel and Tower (Chicago)
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/432_Park_Avenue" title="432 Park Avenue">
       432 Park Avenue
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/One_World_Trade_Center#New_building" title="One World Trade Center">
       new One World Trade Center
      </a>
      . One World Trade Center surpassed the roof height of the Empire State Building on April 30, 2012, and became the tallest building in New York City—on the way toward becoming the tallest building in the Americas at a planned 1,776 feet (541 m).
     </p>
     <p>
      The Empire State Building is currently the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_United_States" title="List of tallest buildings in the United States">
       fifth-tallest completed skyscraper in the United States
      </a>
      , after the
      <a href="/wiki/One_World_Trade_Center" title="One World Trade Center">
       One World Trade Center
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/432_Park_Avenue" title="432 Park Avenue">
       432 Park Avenue
      </a>
      in New York City, the
      <a href="/wiki/Willis_Tower" title="Willis Tower">
       Willis Tower
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Trump_International_Hotel_and_Tower_(Chicago)" title="Trump International Hotel and Tower (Chicago)">
       Trump International Hotel and Tower
      </a>
      , both in
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Chicago" title="List of tallest buildings in Chicago">
       Chicago
      </a>
      . It is also the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_world" title="List of tallest buildings in the world">
       25th-tallest in the world
      </a>
      , the tallest now is
      <a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">
       Burj Khalifa
      </a>
      , located in Dubai. It is also the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_freestanding_structures_in_the_world" title="List of tallest freestanding structures in the world">
       fifth-tallest freestanding structure in the Americas
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      On clear days, the building can be seen from much of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Metropolitan_Area" title="New York Metropolitan Area">
       New York Metropolitan Area
      </a>
      , and as far away as
      <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">
       New Haven, Connecticut
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Morristown,_New_Jersey" title="Morristown, New Jersey">
       Morristown, New Jersey
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Neighboring_Midtown_Manhattan_landmarks">
       Neighboring Midtown Manhattan landmarks
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The Empire State Building anchors an area of Midtown which features other major Manhattan landmarks as well, including
      <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s_Herald_Square" title="Macy's Herald Square">
       Macy's Herald Square
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Koreatown,_Manhattan" title="Koreatown, Manhattan">
       Koreatown
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        [87]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Station_(New_York_City)" title="Pennsylvania Station (New York City)">
       Penn Station
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">
       Madison Square Garden
      </a>
      , and the Flower District.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        [88]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Together, these sites contribute to a significant volume of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commuter" title="Commuter">
       commuter
      </a>
      and tourist
      <a href="/wiki/Pedestrian" title="Pedestrian">
       pedestrian
      </a>
      traffic traversing the southern portion of Midtown Manhattan.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">
       In popular culture
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Film">
       Film
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">

        1933 Movie poster for King Kong
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Img_kingkong1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="253" data-file-width="340" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/88/Img_kingkong1.jpg/220px-Img_kingkong1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/88/Img_kingkong1.jpg/330px-Img_kingkong1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/88/Img_kingkong1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Img_kingkong1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A frame from the 1933 film of
        <a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(1933_film)" title="King Kong (1933 film)">
         King Kong
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Perhaps the most famous popular culture representation of the building is in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(1933_film)" title="King Kong (1933 film)">
         King Kong
        </a>
       </i>
       (1933), in which the title character, a giant ape, climbs to the top to escape his captors but falls to his death after being attacked by airplanes. In 1983, for the film's fiftieth anniversary, a huge 90-foot (27 m) tall inflatable Kong was placed on the building mast above the observation deck by artist Robert Vicino.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WashPo1_91-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WashPo1-91">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2005,
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">
        Peter Jackson
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Remake" title="Remake">
        remake
       </a>
       of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(2005_film)" title="King Kong (2005 film)">
         King Kong
        </a>
       </i>
       was released, set in 1930s New York City, including a final showdown between Kong and biplanes atop a greatly detailed Empire State Building. (The 1976 remake of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(1976_film)" title="King Kong (1976 film)">
         King Kong
        </a>
       </i>
       was set in a contemporary New York City and held its climactic scene on the towers of the World Trade Center.)
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Love_Affair_(1939_film)" title="Love Affair (1939 film)">
         Love Affair
        </a>
       </i>
       (1939) involves a couple who plan to meet atop the Empire State Building, a rendezvous that is prevented by an automobile accident. The film was remade in 1957 (as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/An_Affair_to_Remember" title="An Affair to Remember">
         An Affair to Remember
        </a>
       </i>
       ) and in 1994 (again as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Love_Affair_(1994_film)" title="Love Affair (1994 film)">
         Love Affair
        </a>
       </i>
       ).
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Sleepless_in_Seattle" title="Sleepless in Seattle">
         Sleepless in Seattle
        </a>
       </i>
       (1993), a romantic comedy partially inspired by
       <i>
        An Affair to Remember
       </i>
       , climaxes with scenes in the Empire State Building's lobby and observatory.
      </li>
      <li>
       In the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Looney_Tunes" title="Looney Tunes">
         Looney Tunes
        </a>
       </i>
       cartoon "Much Ado About Nutting", a squirrel has so much difficulty opening a coconut he carries it to the Empire State Building's observation deck and tosses it over the edge. While the street is damaged by the impact, the coconut remains intact.
      </li>
      <li>
       In the 1946
       <i>
        Looney Tunes
       </i>
       cartoon
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Bugs" title="Baseball Bugs">
         Baseball Bugs
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bugs_Bunny" title="Bugs Bunny">
        Bugs Bunny
       </a>
       is pitching in the
       <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds" title="Polo Grounds">
        Polo Grounds
       </a>
       against the Gashouse Gorillas. In the bottom of the ninth, with two outs and Bugs protecting a one run lead, the opposition hits the ball out of the park for an apparent game-winning two-run homer. Bugs pursues the ball through New York City. The chase culminates at the "Umpire State Building". Bugs ascends to the top of the building by elevator and catches the ball for the third out, winning the game.
      </li>
      <li>
       In the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Tom_and_Jerry" title="Tom and Jerry">
         Tom and Jerry
        </a>
       </i>
       cartoon "
       <a href="/wiki/Mouse_in_Manhattan" title="Mouse in Manhattan">
        Mouse in Manhattan
       </a>
       ", Jerry walks by and views the Empire State Building, along with other landmarks, including the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Statue_of_Atlas" title="Statue of Atlas">
        Statue of Atlas
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Center" title="Rockefeller Center">
        Rockefeller Center
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_Terminal" title="Grand Central Terminal">
        Grand Central Terminal
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">
        Andy Warhol
       </a>
       's 1964 silent film
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Empire_(1964_film)" title="Empire (1964 film)">
         Empire
        </a>
       </i>
       is one continuous, eight-hour black-and-white shot of the Empire State Building at night. In 2004, the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Registry" title="National Film Registry">
        National Film Registry
       </a>
       deemed its cultural significance worthy of preservation in the
       <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">
        Library of Congress
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       In
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Percy_Jackson_%26_the_Olympians:_The_Lightning_Thief" title="Percy Jackson &amp; the Olympians: The Lightning Thief">
         Percy Jackson &amp; the Olympians: The Lightning Thief
        </a>
       </i>
       (2010), Mount Olympus is located over the Empire State Building, and there is a special elevator in the building to the "600th floor", which is supposed to be Olympus, just like in the
       <a href="/wiki/Percy_Jackson_%26_the_Olympians" title="Percy Jackson &amp; the Olympians">
        book series
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       The building is chosen as Ground Zero for the target of a nuclear bomb that is dropped on New York in
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fail-Safe_(1964_film)" title="Fail-Safe (1964 film)">
         Fail-Safe
        </a>
       </i>
       (1964).
      </li>
      <li>
       Both
       <a href="/wiki/Zero_Mostel" title="Zero Mostel">
        Zero Mostel
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gene_Wilder" title="Gene Wilder">
        Gene Wilder
       </a>
       go to the Observation Deck of the building in the original
       <a href="/wiki/Mel_Brooks" title="Mel Brooks">
        Mel Brooks
       </a>
       film
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Producers_(1968_film)" title="The Producers (1968 film)">
         The Producers
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       In
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Time_Machine_(2002_film)" title="The Time Machine (2002 film)">
         The Time Machine
        </a>
       </i>
       (2002), the Empire State Building is still standing in the year 2030, but dwarfed by several larger skyscrapers around it. It is not visible in later scenes set in a post-apocalyptic New York.
      </li>
      <li>
       In
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Sky_Captain_and_the_World_of_Tomorrow" title="Sky Captain and the World of Tomorrow">
         Sky Captain and the World of Tomorrow
        </a>
       </i>
       (2004), the top of the building serves its original purpose of being a docking station for dirigibles, and the
       <i>
        Hindenburg III
       </i>
       docks at it on its maiden voyage.
      </li>
      <li>
       The building starred in
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enchanted_(2007_film)" title="Enchanted (2007 film)">
         Enchanted
        </a>
       </i>
       (2007) which Giselle tried to rescue Robert from Queen Narissa in her dragon form.
      </li>
      <li>
       Many films have opened with the Empire State Building, such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/West_Side_Story_(film)" title="West Side Story (film)">
         West Side Story
        </a>
       </i>
       (1961),
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Step_Up_3D" title="Step Up 3D">
         Step Up 3D
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Other_Guys" title="The Other Guys">
         The Other Guys
        </a>
       </i>
       (both 2010).
      </li>
      <li>
       The building has been destroyed in some
       <a href="/wiki/Disaster_film" title="Disaster film">
        disaster films
       </a>
       , such as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(1996_film)" title="Independence Day (1996 film)">
         Independence Day
        </a>
       </i>
       (1996) and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Knowing_(film)" title="Knowing (film)">
         Knowing
        </a>
       </i>
       (2009).
      </li>
      <li>
       In
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Divide_(film)" title="The Divide (film)">
         The Divide
        </a>
       </i>
       (2011), the building is destroyed by a nuclear bomb detonated on New York. It was heavily featured on posters promoting the film.
      </li>
      <li>
       In
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Superman_II" title="Superman II">
         Superman II
        </a>
       </i>
       (1980),
       <a href="/wiki/Ursa_(comics)" title="Ursa (comics)">
        Ursa
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Douglas" title="Sarah Douglas">
        Sarah Douglas
       </a>
       ) uses a flagpole to knock
       <a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">
        Superman
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Reeve" title="Christopher Reeve">
        Christopher Reeve
       </a>
       ) into the tower of the
       <a href="/wiki/Chrysler_Building" title="Chrysler Building">
        Chrysler Building
       </a>
       . He ducks with
       <a href="/wiki/Non_(comics)" title="Non (comics)">
        Non
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Jack_O%27Halloran" title="Jack O'Halloran">
        Jack O'Halloran
       </a>
       ) taking the blast. However, scenes showing the tower falling and being flown back to the top by Superman are of the Empire State Building.
      </li>
      <li>
       In
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_5th_Wave_(film)" title="The 5th Wave (film)">
         The 5th Wave
        </a>
       </i>
       , the building happens to survive a massive tsunami that hits Manhattan during an alien invasion.
      </li>
      <li>
       Many other films that feature the Empire State Building are listed on the building's own website.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Television">
       Television
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       In the 1965 four-part
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Underdog_(TV_series)" title="Underdog (TV series)">
         Underdog
        </a>
       </i>
       cartoon serial "The Phoney Booths" (episodes 49-52),
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Underdog_characters#Underdog" title="List of Underdog characters">
        Underdog
       </a>
       falls under the mental control of mad scientist
       <a href="/wiki/Simon_Bar_Sinister" title="Simon Bar Sinister">
        Simon Bar Sinister
       </a>
       . Simon orders Underdog to use his super powers to bring him valuable objects - including the Empire State Building, which Underdog lifts whole to bring it to Simon. In the end, circumstances release Underdog from Simon’s control. He defeats the evil scientist and puts back the Empire State Building.
      </li>
      <li>
       The Empire State Building featured in the 1966
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">
         Doctor Who
        </a>
       </i>
       serial
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Chase_(Doctor_Who)" title="The Chase (Doctor Who)">
         The Chase
        </a>
       </i>
       , in which the
       <a href="/wiki/TARDIS" title="TARDIS">
        TARDIS
       </a>
       lands on the roof of the building;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doctor_(Doctor_Who)" title="Doctor (Doctor Who)">
        The Doctor
       </a>
       and his companions leave quite quickly, however, because
       <a href="/wiki/Dalek" title="Dalek">
        The Daleks
       </a>
       are close behind them. A Dalek is also seen on the roof of the building while it interrogates a human. In 2007,
       <i>
        Doctor Who
       </i>
       episodes "
       <a href="/wiki/Daleks_in_Manhattan" title="Daleks in Manhattan">
        Daleks in Manhattan
       </a>
       " and "
       <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_the_Daleks" title="Evolution of the Daleks">
        Evolution of the Daleks
       </a>
       " also featured the building, which
       <a href="/wiki/Dalek" title="Dalek">
        the Daleks
       </a>
       are constructing to use as a lightning conductor.
       <a href="/wiki/Russell_T_Davies" title="Russell T Davies">
        Russell T Davies
       </a>
       said in an article that "in his mind", the Daleks remembered the building from their last visit.
      </li>
      <li>
       In the science fiction drama series
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Fringe_(TV_series)" title="Fringe (TV series)">
         Fringe
        </a>
       </i>
       , the observation deck of the Empire State Building serves its primary purpose as a docking station for zeppelins in the parallel universe shown in the second-season episode
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Peter_(Fringe)#Cultural_references" title="Peter (Fringe)">
         Peter
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Channel" title="Discovery Channel">
        Discovery Channel
       </a>
       show
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/MythBusters_(2003_season)#Penny_Drop" title="MythBusters (2003 season)">
         MythBusters
        </a>
       </i>
       tested the urban myth which claims that if one drops a penny off the top of the Empire State Building, it could kill someone or put a crater in the pavement. The outcome was that, by the time the penny hits the ground, it is going roughly 65 mph (105 km/h) (
       <a href="/wiki/Terminal_velocity" title="Terminal velocity">
        terminal velocity
       </a>
       for an object of its mass and shape), which is not fast enough to inflict lethal injury or put a crater into the pavement. The urban legend is a joke in the 2003 musical
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Avenue_Q" title="Avenue Q">
         Avenue Q
        </a>
       </i>
       , where a character waiting atop the building for a rendezvous tosses a penny over the side—only to hit her rival.
      </li>
      <li>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Anderson" title="Gerry Anderson">
        Gerry Anderson
       </a>
       's popular puppet series
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Thunderbirds_(TV_series)" title="Thunderbirds (TV series)">
         Thunderbirds
        </a>
        ,
       </i>
       the episode
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Terror_in_New_York_City" title="Terror in New York City">
         Terror in New York City
        </a>
       </i>
       , the Empire State Building is being moved to a new location as the site around it is set for redevelopment. However, something goes wrong and the building collapses, trapping a reporter and his cameraman underneath the rubble. Their rescue is the focus of the rest of the episode.
      </li>
      <li>
       The music video of the song "Everything is Everything" (by singer
       <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">
        Lauryn Hill
       </a>
       ) prominently features the Empire State Building as the center of a city (record) turntable.
      </li>
      <li>
       In the episode "
       <a href="/wiki/First_Time_in_New_York" title="First Time in New York">
        First Time in New York
       </a>
       " of the television series
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/How_I_Met_Your_Mother" title="How I Met Your Mother">
         How I Met Your Mother
        </a>
       </i>
       (originally aired on January 8, 2007), the gang takes Robin's sister Katie to the Empire State Building. On the first day, they only got to the lobby, but they eventually went to the top the next day.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">
       Literature
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/H.G._Wells" title="H.G. Wells">
        H.G. Wells
       </a>
       ' 1933 science fiction novel
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Shape_of_Things_to_Come" title="The Shape of Things to Come">
         The Shape of Things to Come
        </a>
       </i>
       , written in the form of a
       <a href="/wiki/Future_history" title="Future history">
        history book published in the far future
       </a>
       , includes the following passage: "Up to quite recently Lower New York has been the most old-fashioned city in the world, unique in its gloomy antiquity. The last of the ancient skyscrapers, the Empire State Building, is even now under demolition in C.E. 2106!".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/David_Macaulay" title="David Macaulay">
        David Macaulay
       </a>
       's 1980 illustrated book
       <i>
        Unbuilding
       </i>
       depicts the Empire State Building being purchased by a Middle Eastern billionaire and disassembled piece by piece, to be transported to Saudi Arabia and rebuilt there. The mooring mast is rebuilt in New York, while the remainder of the building is lost at sea.
      </li>
      <li>
       Giannina
       <a href="/wiki/Braschi%27s_Empire_of_Dreams" title="Braschi's Empire of Dreams">
        Braschi's Empire of Dreams
       </a>
       , a Latin American poetry epic published in 1988, featured a pastoral revolution on the top floor of the Empire State Building, where shepherds danced and sang songs of revolution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marting_167.E2.80.93182_75-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Marting_167.E2.80.93182-75">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       The Empire State Building is featured prominently as both a setting and integral plot device throughout much of
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Chabon" title="Michael Chabon">
        Michael Chabon
       </a>
       's 2000
       <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">
        Pulitzer Prize
       </a>
       -winning novel,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Adventures_of_Kavalier_%26_Clay" title="The Amazing Adventures of Kavalier &amp; Clay">
         The Amazing Adventures of Kavalier &amp; Clay
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       In his "biography",
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Doc_Savage:_His_Apocalyptic_Life" title="Doc Savage: His Apocalyptic Life">
         Doc Savage: His Apocalyptic Life
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philip_Jose_Farmer" title="Philip Jose Farmer">
        Philip Jose Farmer
       </a>
       theorizes that the skyscraper in which
       <a href="/wiki/Doc_Savage" title="Doc Savage">
        Doc Savage
       </a>
       lived and where he met with his comrades, had his laboratories,
       <i>
        etc.
       </i>
       , was the Empire State Building. Since the 86th Floor (mentioned in the Savage stories as his floor) was the Observatory, one may presume that Doc "actually" lived on another floor.
      </li>
      <li>
       In the series, "
       <a href="/wiki/Percy_Jackson_%26_the_Olympians" title="Percy Jackson &amp; the Olympians">
        Percy Jackson &amp; the Olympians
       </a>
       ",
       <a href="/wiki/Rick_Riordan" title="Rick Riordan">
        Rick Riordan
       </a>
       shows the Empire State Building as the headquarters of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympian_Gods" title="Olympian Gods">
        Olympian Gods
       </a>
       , where the Greek Gods live and also hold their meetings.
      </li>
      <li>
       In the 1961 children's novel
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/James_and_the_Giant_Peach" title="James and the Giant Peach">
         James and the Giant Peach
        </a>
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Roald_Dahl" title="Roald Dahl">
        Roald Dahl
       </a>
       , the giant peach is dropped onto the lightning rod of the Empire State Building at the end. This novel was later adapted in a
       <a href="/wiki/James_and_the_Giant_Peach_(film)" title="James and the Giant Peach (film)">
        film under the same name
       </a>
       in 1996, which features the same part where the peach falls on to the Building's antenna.
      </li>
      <li>
       In the sci-fi/alternate history series of novels
       <a href="/wiki/Wild_Cards" title="Wild Cards">
        Wild Cards
       </a>
       , the 86th floor is the location of New York's premier chic restaurant, Aces High, a very popular hangout for the superpowered aces.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other">
       Other
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       A 7.6 feet (2.3 m) scale model built from 12,000 LEGO bricks over 250 hours is featured along with other notable buildings in the
       <i>
        LEGO Architecture: Towering Ambition
       </i>
       exhibition at the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Building_Museum" title="National Building Museum">
        National Building Museum
       </a>
       in Washington, D.C.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       The Empire State Building Run-Up is a foot race from ground level to the 86th-floor observation deck that has been held annually since 1978. Its participants are referred to both as runners and as climbers, and are often
       <a href="/wiki/Tower_running" title="Tower running">
        tower running
       </a>
       enthusiasts. The race covers a vertical distance of 1,050 feet (320 m) and takes in 1,576 steps. The record time is 9 minutes and 33 seconds, achieved by Australian professional cyclist
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_Crake" title="Paul Crake">
        Paul Crake
       </a>
       in 2003,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       at a climbing rate of 6,593 ft (2,010 m) per hour.
      </li>
     </ul>

           Current

           </a>
           , Suite 6905
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
            <a href="#cite_note-98">
             [96]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Boy_Scouts_of_America" title="Boy Scouts of America">
            Boy Scouts of America
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Greater_New_York_Councils" title="Greater New York Councils">

           </a>
           , Suite 430
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">

            </a>

          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Coty,_Inc." title="Coty, Inc.">

        <span class="reference-text">

           "The Day A Bomber Hit The Empire State Building"
          </a>
          . NPR
          <span class="reference-accessdate">

          <q>
           Eight months after the crash, the U.S. government offered money to families of the victims. Some accepted, but others initiated a lawsuit that resulted in landmark legislation. The Federal Tort Claims Act of 1946, for the first time, gave American citizens the right to sue the federal government.

          </a>
          .
          <i>
           Circumference Magazine: Poetry in Translation, Academy of American Poets
          </i>
          . January 1, 2013.

           ’Considered one of the most revolutionary Latin American poets writing today, Giannina Braschi, author of the epic prose poem Empire of Dreams’
